You said:
Master Blueprint: French Factur-X Converter SaaS
1. The Core Mission
To build a "Compliance Bridge" for the French B2B market that allows small businesses (TPE/PME) to comply with the 2026 PPF (Portail Public de Facturation) e-invoicing mandate without replacing their current invoicing software.

The Problem: Millions of businesses generate standard PDFs (via Word, Excel, or legacy ERPs) which are illegal under the new mandate because they are not machine-readable.

The Solution: A web-based tool that accepts a standard PDF and "upgrades" it into a Factur-X (PDF/A-3) file by embedding the mandatory structured XML data inside it.

2. The Architecture (The "How")
Input Layer: A simple drag-and-drop interface for standard PDFs.

Processing Layer (The Engine): A Python-based backend that reads the PDF stream and merges it with a generated XML file based on the Factur-X Minimum or Basic profile standards.

Compliance Layer: Adheres to the EN 16931 European standard for electronic invoicing.

Tech Stack:

Logic: Python 3.12 (Selected for robust file manipulation libraries).

Interface: Streamlit (Selected for rapid UI development and Python integration).

Core Libraries: factur-x (Standard compliance), pypdf (PDF manipulation).

3. The Competitive Landscape
The Giants (Pennylane, Libeo, Doctolib): All-in-one accounting suites that require full migration and subscriptions.

The "Gap": There are very few lightweight tools that allow a business to keep their old Word/Excel habits while still becoming compliant.

Your Moat: Simplicity and friction-free compliance. No "onboarding," just file conversion.

🗺️ The Master Roadmap
This roadmap takes you from the current local prototype to a sellable SaaS product.

Phase 1: The Foundation (Completed ✅)
Goal: Prove the technology works.

Status: Operational Local MVP.

Achievement: Successfully resolved environment conflicts ("Two Pythons" issue) and generated a valid Factur-X PDF with embedded XML on a local machine using hard-coded/manual metadata.

Phase 2: Intelligence & Automation (Current Priority)
Goal: Eliminate manual data entry to increase user speed.

Action: Integrate OCR (Optical Character Recognition).

Implementation: Connect an API (like Azure Document Intelligence, AWS Textract, or OpenAI Vision) to automatically read the Invoice Number, Date, Buyer Name, and Total Amount from the uploaded PDF so the user doesn't have to type them.

Phase 3: Validation & Compliance (The "Trust" Layer)
Goal: Guarantee that the files are legally valid.

Action: Build a "Validator" step that runs the generated XML against the official Chorus Pro XSD schemas.

Value: If a file fails validation, the user is warned before they download it, preventing rejection by the government portal.

Phase 4: Production & Deployment
Goal: Move from "Localhost" to the Web.

Action: Containerize the application (Docker) and deploy to a cloud host (Streamlit Cloud, Railway, or Render).

Requirement: Set up a requirements.txt environment that replicates the local fix we engineered.

Phase 5: Monetization (SaaS)
Goal: Turn the tool into a business.

Features:

Freemium Model: 5 free conversions/month.

Pro Model: Unlimited conversions + Bulk processing (upload 50 PDFs at once).

API Access: Allow other software developers to use your engine for a fee.

🛑 Critical Note for Developers
Environment Sensitivity: This project relies on the factur-x library, which has strict dependency requirements (specifically lxml and reportlab).

Execution Rule: Always ensure the runtime environment targets the exact Python executable where these libraries are installed to avoid ModuleNotFoundError. Use absolute paths for pip installation and execution commands.

From 1 Sept 2026 (large & mid-size) and 1 Sept 2027 (all companies), French domestic B2B invoices must be electronic and structured. Accepted formats: UBL 2.1, UN/CEFACT CII, and Factur‑X (hybrid PDF+XML, EN 16931‑compliant).

2.3. Minimal “invoice extraction” service (Python)
Install:

The core usage is:
Create a DocumentIntelligenceClient with endpoint + key.

+1
Call begin_analyze_document("prebuilt-invoice", body=<file-like>). 
Microsoft Learn
+1
Read result.documents[0].fields[...] for InvoiceId, InvoiceDate, etc. 
azuresdkdocs.z19.web.core.windows.net
+1
Here’s a clean wrapper module:
# services/ocr_azure.py
from __future__ import annotations

import io
from typing import Dict, Optional

from azure.core.credentials import AzureKeyCredential
from azure.ai.documentintelligence import DocumentIntelligenceClient


class AzureInvoiceExtractor:
    def __init__(self, endpoint: str, api_key: str) -> None:
        self._client = DocumentIntelligenceClient(
            endpoint=endpoint,
            credential=AzureKeyCredential(api_key),
        )

    def extract_header(self, pdf_bytes: bytes) -> Dict[str, Optional[str]]:
        """
        Returns a dict with best-effort values (or None) for:
        invoice_number, invoice_date (ISO str), buyer_name, total_amount.
        """
        # Body can be an IO[bytes]
        stream = io.BytesIO(pdf_bytes)

        poller = self._client.begin_analyze_document(
            model_id="prebuilt-invoice",
            body=stream,
            locale="fr-FR",   # Hint: it's a French invoice
        )
        result = poller.result()

        if not result.documents:
            return {
                "invoice_number": None,
                "invoice_date": None,
                "buyer_name": None,
                "total_amount": None,
            }

        doc = result.documents[0]
        fields = doc.fields or {}

        def _take_first(field, keys):
            if not field:
                return None
            for k in keys:
                if k in field and field[k] is not None:
                    return str(field[k])
            return None

        invoice_id = _take_first(fields.get("InvoiceId"), ("valueString", "content"))
        invoice_date = _take_first(fields.get("InvoiceDate"), ("valueDate", "valueString", "content"))
        customer_name = _take_first(fields.get("CustomerName"), ("valueString", "content"))
        invoice_total = _take_first(fields.get("InvoiceTotal"), ("content", "valueNumber", "valueString"))

        return {
            "invoice_number": invoice_id,
            "invoice_date": invoice_date,
            "buyer_name": customer_name,
            "total_amount": invoice_total,
        }
Notes:
This is slightly defensive, because the field payload is dict‑like (valueString, valueDate, content etc.). 
azuresdkdocs.z19.web.core.windows.net
+1
You can also read field.confidence and later surface low‑confidence fields in red in the UI.
2.4. Wiring this into Streamlit
Your happy path UX:
User uploads PDF.
We immediately run OCR and show a spinner.
We pre‑fill the metadata form with the extracted values (user can correct them).
On submit, we generate XML + Factur‑X and show a download button.
Example streamlit_app.py:
# streamlit_app.py
from __future__ import annotations

import os
import tempfile
from datetime import date
from decimal import Decimal, InvalidOperation

import streamlit as st
from facturx import generate_from_file, xml_check_xsd  # from factur-x library

from services.ocr_azure import AzureInvoiceExtractor


st.set_page_config(page_title="Factur‑X Converter", layout="centered")

st.title("Factur‑X Converter – Pont de conformité 🇫🇷")

# Ideally store these in Streamlit secrets, not env vars
AZURE_ENDPOINT = st.secrets["AZURE_DI_ENDPOINT"]
AZURE_KEY = st.secrets["AZURE_DI_KEY"]

extractor = AzureInvoiceExtractor(AZURE_ENDPOINT, AZURE_KEY)

uploaded = st.file_uploader("Déposez votre facture PDF", type=["pdf"])

if uploaded:
    pdf_bytes = uploaded.read()

    with st.spinner("Lecture automatique de la facture..."):
        auto = extractor.extract_header(pdf_bytes)

    st.subheader("1. Vérifiez les informations extraites")

    col1, col2 = st.columns(2)
    invoice_number = col1.text_input(
        "Numéro de facture",
        value=auto.get("invoice_number") or "",
    )

    # basic date parsing; you can refine this
    default_date = date.today()
    if auto.get("invoice_date"):
        try:
            default_date = date.fromisoformat(str(auto["invoice_date"])[:10])
        except Exception:
            pass

    invoice_date = col2.date_input(
        "Date de facture",
        value=default_date,
        format="DD/MM/YYYY",
    )

    buyer_name = st.text_input(
        "Client (dénomination)",
        value=auto.get("buyer_name") or "",
    )

    total_amount_str = st.text_input(
        "Montant TTC",
        value=auto.get("total_amount") or "",
    )

    st.caption("Les champs sont pré‑remplis, mais vous pouvez les corriger avant génération.")

    st.subheader("2. Générer la facture Factur‑X")

    if st.button("Générer le PDF Factur‑X"):
        # --- 2.1 Build your XML here (existing logic) ---
        try:
            total_amount = Decimal(total_amount_str.replace(",", "."))
        except (InvalidOperation, AttributeError):
            st.error("Montant TTC invalide – utilisez seulement des chiffres, virgule ou point.")
            st.stop()

        xml_bytes = build_facturx_xml_minimum(
            invoice_number=invoice_number,
            invoice_date=invoice_date,
            buyer_name=buyer_name,
            total_amount=total_amount,
        )

        # Optional: validate XML before embedding
        try:
            xml_check_xsd(xml_bytes, flavor="factur-x", level="minimum")
            st.success("XML Factur‑X valide selon le schéma XSD officiel ✅")
        except Exception as e:
            st.error(f"XML NON VALIDE : {e}")
            st.stop()

        # --- 2.2 Merge XML into original PDF ---
        facturx_pdf_bytes = generate_facturx_pdf(pdf_bytes, xml_bytes)

        st.download_button(
            label="Télécharger le PDF Factur‑X",
            data=facturx_pdf_bytes,
            file_name="facture-facturx.pdf",
            mime="application/pdf",
        )
And a simple helper to call factur-x (file‑based interface):
import os
import tempfile
from facturx import generate_from_file

def generate_facturx_pdf(pdf_bytes: bytes, xml_bytes: bytes) -> bytes:
    # Use temp files because generate_from_file works with paths. :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}
    with tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".pdf", delete=False) as pdf_tmp:
        pdf_tmp.write(pdf_bytes)
        pdf_path = pdf_tmp.name

    with tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".xml", delete=False) as xml_tmp:
        xml_tmp.write(xml_bytes)
        xml_path = xml_tmp.name

    out_fd, out_path = tempfile.mkstemp(suffix=".pdf")
    os.close(out_fd)

    generate_from_file(pdf_path, xml_path, output_pdf_file=out_path)

    with open(out_path, "rb") as f:
        out_bytes = f.read()

    for path in (pdf_path, xml_path, out_path):
        try:
            os.remove(path)
        except OSError:
            pass

    return out_bytes

3. Phase 3 – Validator & “Trust layer”
You want a “Validator” step so users don’t download a PDF that will be rejected by the PA/PPF. Good news: the factur-x library already bundles the official XSDs for each profile (MINIMUM, BASIC WL, BASIC, EN16931, EXTENDED) and exposes xml_check_xsd() to validate an XML against the right schema. 
4gl.fr
+1
3.1. Simple validation service
# services/validator.py
from __future__ import annotations

from facturx import xml_check_xsd


class FacturXValidationError(Exception):
    pass


def validate_facturx(xml_bytes: bytes, level: str = "minimum") -> None:
    """
    Raises FacturXValidationError if invalid, returns None if OK.
    """
    try:
        # flavor autodetects Factur-X vs Order-X, but we force it for safety
        xml_check_xsd(xml_bytes, flavor="factur-x", level=level)
    except Exception as exc:
        # xml_check_xsd throws helpful messages when XSD validation fails. :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14}
        raise FacturXValidationError(str(exc)) from exc
3.2. UI flow
In Streamlit:
Generate XML from metadata.
Run validate_facturx(xml_bytes, level="minimum").
If error → show details + do not show the download button.
If success → show green “valid” badge and the download button.
For higher tiers later you might:
Offer “Basic WL” and “Basic” profile selection (toggle in the UI).
Run validation with level="basicwl" / "basic".
Show which fields are missing to reach a higher profile (“Add VAT breakdown to reach BASIC”, etc.).

pypdf==5.1.0

# OCR

azure-core==1.30.0
aiohttp==3.10.5

# Web

4.2. Minimal Dockerfile (Streamlit on Python 3.12)
FROM python:3.12-slim

# Avoid interactive prompts
ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive \
    PYTHONUNBUFFERED=1 \
    PIP_NO_CACHE_DIR=1

# System deps for lxml, reportlab, pypdf fonts, etc.
RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends \
        build-essential \
        libxml2-dev \
        libxslt1-dev \
        libjpeg-dev \
        zlib1g-dev \
    && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*

WORKDIR /app

COPY requirements.txt .
RUN python -m pip install --upgrade pip \
    && python -m pip install -r requirements.txt

# Copy your app
COPY . .

# Streamlit config
ENV STREAMLIT_SERVER_PORT=8501 \
    STREAMLIT_SERVER_HEADLESS=true

EXPOSE 8501

CMD ["streamlit", "run", "streamlit_app.py"]
Deployment options that fit your stack:
Streamlit Community Cloud – very easy, but limited for a commercial SaaS.
Railway / Render / Fly.io / Azure App Service – good balance of simplicity and control.
If you later build an API for partners, you can put FastAPI behind a separate container and call your Factur‑X engine as a shared library.
5. Phase 5 – Monetization / SaaS mechanics
You already have the product; monetization is mostly rate limits + authentication around the same engine.
5.1. Basic account model
Add a tiny auth layer (FastAPI or a simple Streamlit auth integration):
Users table: id, email, plan (free|pro), api_key, current_period_conversions, period_start.
On each conversion:
Increment current_period_conversions.
If plan = free and current_period_conversions > 5 → show paywall.
Reset counters monthly with a cron or simple “if now > period_start + 30d then reset”.
5.2. Bulk processing
For Pro:
Extend the UI to support multi‑file upload (Streamlit: accept_multiple_files=True in file_uploader).
Iterate over each file, call the same pipeline, zip results:
import io
import zipfile

z_buf = io.BytesIO()
with zipfile.ZipFile(z_buf, "w", zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED) as zf:
    for uploaded in uploaded_files:
        pdf_bytes = uploaded.read()
        # ... extract metadata (or skip to manual), build XML, validate ...
        fx_bytes = generate_facturx_pdf(pdf_bytes, xml_bytes)
        zf.writestr(f"{uploaded.name[:-4]}-facturx.pdf", fx_bytes)

z_buf.seek(0)
st.download_button(
    "Télécharger toutes les factures Factur‑X (ZIP)",
    data=z_buf,
    file_name="facturx_batch.zip",
    mime="application/zip",
)
5.3. Public API
Once your engine is stable, expose a simple REST API: POST /v1/convert
Body: multipart/form-data with pdf and optional JSON override for fields.
Response: application/pdf (Factur‑X) or JSON error with validation messages.
Billing: count API conversions exactly like UI conversions.
Internally the API code literally calls the same functions you use for Streamlit: extractor.extract_header -> build_facturx_xml -> validate_facturx -> generate_facturx_pdf.

2. Clean up old Python and install Python 3.12 (Windows)
Step 2.1 – Check if Python is already installed
Click the Start (Windows) button.
Type cmd.
Click “Command Prompt” (black window).
In the black window, type:
python --version
Press Enter.
If you see something like Python 3.10.4 or Python 3.11.2, Python exists.
If it says “not recognized”, Python is not in your PATH (or not installed).
Step 2.2 – Uninstall old Python (simple way)
You don’t have to uninstall old Python, but to avoid the “two Python” confusion, it’s easier for you.
Click Start → Settings → Apps → Installed apps (or “Apps & Features”).
In the search box, type “Python”.
For each “Python 3.x” you see:
Click it
Click Uninstall and follow the steps.

4. Create your first project folder
We’ll create a small folder for your Factur‑X project. Think of it as one binder for this idea.
Step 4.1 – Create folders
Open File Explorer.
Go to somewhere simple, like Documents.
Create a new folder called:
facturx_project
Inside that folder, create two folders:

├─ input
└─ output

5. Create a “virtual environment” (a private Python world)
A virtual environment is like a separate mini‑Python just for this project.
This avoids breaking other things and keeps all your libraries together.
Step 5.1 – Open the VS Code terminal
In VS Code, click Terminal → New Terminal.
A terminal will open at the bottom.
You should see something like:
C:\Users\YourName\Documents\facturx_project>
Step 5.2 – Create the virtual environment
In the terminal, type:
python -m venv venv
This creates a folder called venv (hidden by VS Code by default) that holds your private Python.
Step 5.3 – Activate the virtual environment (Windows)
Type:
venv\Scripts\activate
After that, you should see something like:
(venv) C:\Users\YourName\Documents\facturx_project>

9. Create the Python script that does the glueing
Now we write a tiny Python program that:
Reads input/sample_invoice.pdf
Reads input/sample_invoice.xml
Uses factur-x to glue them together into

Step 9.1 – Create convert.py
In VS Code, right‑click on the main folder facturx_project.
Click New File.
Name it:
convert.py
Paste this code:
from pathlib import Path

# Import the function from the factur-x library
from facturx import generate_from_file  # library that glues XML into the PDF


def main():
    # 1. Define paths
    base_dir = Path(__file__).parent
    input_dir = base_dir / "input"
    output_dir = base_dir / "output"

    pdf_path = input_dir / "sample_invoice.pdf"
    xml_path = input_dir / "sample_invoice.xml"
    output_pdf_path = output_dir / "sample_invoice_facturx.pdf"

    # 2. Check files exist
    if not pdf_path.exists():
        print("❌ I cannot find input/sample_invoice.pdf")
        print("   Please put your invoice PDF in the 'input' folder and name it sample_invoice.pdf")
        return

    if not xml_path.exists():
        print("❌ I cannot find input/sample_invoice.xml")
        print("   Please create that XML file first.")
        return

    # 3. Make sure output folder exists
    output_dir.mkdir(exist_ok=True)

    # 4. Use factur-x to generate the new PDF with embedded XML
    print("🔧 Creating Factur-X style PDF (embedding XML)...")
    generate_from_file(
        str(pdf_path),
        str(xml_path),
        output_pdf_file=str(output_pdf_path),
    )

    print("✅ Done!")
    print(f"   New file created: {output_pdf_path}")


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
What this does in human words:
generate_from_file(...) is the magic function from the factur-x library.
It reads your original PDF and XML file and writes a PDF where the XML is embedded according to the Factur‑X way. 
PyPI
+1

Thought for 9m 29s
Let’s zoom out and tell the whole story like we’re explaining it to a smart 10‑year‑old… who also happens to care about French VAT 😄
1. The Story: What’s happening in France?
1.1. Before: “PDF is enough”
For years, in most French companies:
You made invoices in Word, Excel, or your ERP.
You clicked “Export as PDF”.
You emailed that PDF to your customer.
Your accountant (or their software) typed the numbers again by hand.
The government didn’t really care how the invoice looked, as long as the totals and VAT were correct. These PDFs are like photos of the invoice:
Humans can read them.
But computers are almost blind: they just see pixels or text, not “Ah, this is the invoice number, this is the VAT, this is the buyer”.
1.2. Now: France wants smart invoices, not just pretty ones
From 1 September 2026, France is rolling out a system where B2B invoices must be electronic and structured for VAT purposes.
SEEBURGER
+1
 That means:
Every business must be able to receive a structured e‑invoice from that date.
Big and mid‑size businesses must send structured e‑invoices from 2026.
Small ones (TPE/PME) must follow from 2027.
SEEBURGER
+1
And crucial detail:
France only accepts 3 formats for these structured invoices:
ClearTax
+1
UBL (pure XML)
CII (pure XML)
Factur‑X (PDF + XML hybrid)
So:
Plain PDFs (only visual) will not be compliant anymore for domestic B2B invoices.
They must contain structured data that a machine can read.
1.3. And Factur‑X is… what exactly?
Think of Factur‑X as a “two‑in‑one invoice”:
FNFE-MPE
+2
Maginvoice - create invoices
+2
On the outside: a normal PDF that humans see (looks like your usual invoice).
On the inside: a hidden XML file that machines understand (fields like InvoiceNumber, TotalAmount, VAT amount, etc.) following the European EN 16931 standard.
FNFE-MPE
+2
Weproc
+2
So one Factur‑X file =
“PDF for humans + XML for robots”, packed together.
Factur‑X comes in profiles, like difficulty levels:
ProAbono
+2
Vat Update
+2
Minimum – just the key info: buyer, seller, totals, VAT.
Basic WL (“Without Lines”) – header + totals, no line details.
Basic – same + simplified invoice lines.
EN 16931 – full detail, ERP‑friendly.
Extended – even more info for specific industries.
For a TPE/PME just trying to obey the law, Minimum or Basic WL is often enough at the start.
1.4. The new plumbing in the background
Before, you could email invoices directly to clients. Soon, the flow will be more like this:
vatcalc.com
+3
impots.gouv.fr
+3
Tradeshift
+3
You create a structured invoice (like Factur‑X).
You send it via a certified platform (a PDP / Partner Dematerialization Platform, or “Plateforme Agréée”).
That platform:
Checks the data.
Sends the invoice to the buyer’s platform.
Sends VAT‑related data to the government’s system.
So invoices become like trains passing through a central railway network, not random emails going everywhere.
2. Your Idea: The “Compliance Bridge”
Now, your idea is very clever:
Problem: Millions of French businesses are used to Word/Excel/PDF.
They don’t want to migrate to big platforms like Pennylane, Libeo, Sage, etc.
Law: They must send structured invoices (like Factur‑X).
Plain PDFs will be refused by platforms / buyers.
Your product:
A web tool where they upload their normal PDF, and it returns a Factur‑X PDF which is compliant.
So your tool sits in the middle as a bridge:
Old habits (Word/Excel + PDF) → your bridge → Factur‑X (PDF + XML) → PDP / government.
No change to their internal process, no ERP migration, no full accounting suite.
Just file in, file out. That’s your moat: simple, focused, zero onboarding.
3. How we build this bridge (concept first, then practice)
Let’s now connect the story to the technical bits you saw.
3.1. What has to happen inside your tool?
For each invoice, your engine must do three things:
Read the original PDF
This is the “human‑visible” part.
Create the XML data that describes the invoice in EN 16931 style
Includes things like:
Seller VAT number
Buyer VAT number
Invoice number
Date
Amounts (HT, VAT, TTC)
Line items (if you go beyond Minimum / Basic WL)
Glue the XML into the PDF in the Factur‑X way
This creates a PDF/A‑3 file that contains the XML as an attachment and marks itself as Factur‑X with a profile (Minimum, Basic WL, etc.).
The good news:
There are already Python libraries that know how to glue XML into PDFs according to Factur‑X. You don’t have to reinvent that.

Once you see that working, everything else is “just” adding layers.

from pathlib import Path
from facturx import generate_from_file  # library that glues XML into the PDF

def main():
    base_dir = Path(__file__).parent
    input_dir = base_dir / "input"
    output_dir = base_dir / "output"

    pdf_path = input_dir / "sample_invoice.pdf"
    xml_path = input_dir / "sample_invoice.xml"
    output_pdf_path = output_dir / "sample_invoice_facturx.pdf"

    if not pdf_path.exists():
        print("❌ Missing input/sample_invoice.pdf")
        return

    if not xml_path.exists():
        print("❌ Missing input/sample_invoice.xml")
        return

    output_dir.mkdir(exist_ok=True)

    print("🔧 Embedding XML into PDF (Factur‑X style)...")
    generate_from_file(
        str(pdf_path),
        str(xml_path),
        output_pdf_file=str(output_pdf_path),
    )

    print("✅ Done! Created:", output_pdf_path)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
Conceptually, this does:
Find the sample_invoice.pdf and sample_invoice.xml.
Ask the Factur‑X library to embed the XML in the PDF.
Save the new file into output.

Thought for 3m 27s
Got it — your screenshot shows a very common Windows / PowerShell problem.
What the error means (kid version)
You tried to “turn on” your project’s mini‑Python world (the virtual environment).
But PowerShell is being extra strict and says:
“I don’t allow running script files (like Activate.ps1) on this computer.”
So the venv exists, but PowerShell is refusing to run the activation script. Good news: this is easy to fix. You have 3 safe options. Pick Option A (easiest).
✅ Option A (Easiest): Use Command Prompt instead of PowerShell
This avoids the PowerShell script restriction completely.
In VS Code:
Open VS Code → Terminal at the bottom.
Click the little dropdown arrow next to the + (New Terminal).
Choose Command Prompt (or “cmd”).
Now run this:
venv\Scripts\activate.bat
If it works, your terminal will start with something like:
(venv) C:\Users\...
✅ That means the virtual environment is ON.
✅ Option B: Fix it in PowerShell for this session only (safe + temporary)
If you want to stay in PowerShell, do this:
Step 1: Allow scripts only for this terminal session
Run:
Set-ExecutionPolicy -Scope Process -ExecutionPolicy Bypass
Step 2: Activate venv (PowerShell version)
Run exactly this (important: there is a dot + space at the start):
. .\venv\Scripts\Activate.ps1
If it works, you’ll see (venv) in front of your path. ✅ This change is temporary. When you close the terminal, it goes back to strict mode.
✅ Option C: Fix it permanently for your Windows user (still safe)
If you don’t want to deal with this again:
Set-ExecutionPolicy -Scope CurrentUser -ExecutionPolicy RemoteSigned
Then activate:
. .\venv\Scripts\Activate.ps1
This means:
Scripts you write on your computer can run.
Downloaded scripts must be “trusted/signed”.
⚠️ If this is a work laptop managed by IT, this might be blocked. If it’s blocked, use Option A.
Quick check: Are you in the right folder?
Your screenshot shows:

from pathlib import Path
from facturx import generate_from_file

def main():
    base_dir = Path(__file__).parent

    pdf_path = base_dir / "input" / "sample_invoice.pdf"
    xml_path = base_dir / "input" / "sample_invoice.xml"
    out_path = base_dir / "output" / "sample_invoice_facturx.pdf"

    if not pdf_path.exists():
        print("❌ Missing:", pdf_path)
        return

    if not xml_path.exists():
        print("❌ Missing:", xml_path)
        return

    out_path.parent.mkdir(exist_ok=True)

    print("🔧 Embedding XML into PDF...")
    generate_from_file(str(pdf_path), str(xml_path), output_pdf_file=str(out_path))

    print("✅ Done! Created:", out_path)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

You’re very close now ✅ — and this new error is actually the correct next problem.
What this error means (simple)
Your script is running and it successfully found:
input/sample_invoice.pdf ✅
input/sample_invoice.xml ✅
But the factur-x library is now saying:
“The XML you gave me is NOT a Factur‑X / ZUGFeRD XML… so I can’t recognize it.”
That’s because your XML right now is this kind of “toy XML”:
<Invoice>
  <Date>2025-01-01</Date>
  ...
</Invoice>
But Factur‑X expects a very specific XML shape called CrossIndustryInvoice with special “namespace” names like rsm: and ram: and (most importantly) this ID: urn:factur-x.eu:1p0:minimum The library only works if the XML is Factur‑X compliant. 
PyPI
✅ Fix: Replace your XML with a real Factur‑X Minimum XML template
Step 1 — Open this file in VS Code
Open: input/sample_invoice.xml
Step 2 — Delete everything inside
Select all → delete.
Step 3 — Paste this XML instead (copy-paste exactly)
This is a Minimum profile Factur‑X XML example structure (CrossIndustryInvoice). 
GitHub
+1
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<rsm:CrossIndustryInvoice
  xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
  xmlns:qdt="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:QualifiedDataType:100"
  xmlns:udt="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:UnqualifiedDataType:100"
  xmlns:rsm="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:CrossIndustryInvoice:100"
  xmlns:ram="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:ReusableAggregateBusinessInformationEntity:100">

  <rsm:ExchangedDocumentContext>
    <ram:BusinessProcessSpecifiedDocumentContextParameter>
      <ram:ID>A1</ram:ID>
    </ram:BusinessProcessSpecifiedDocumentContextParameter>

    <ram:GuidelineSpecifiedDocumentContextParameter>
      <ram:ID>urn:factur-x.eu:1p0:minimum</ram:ID>
    </ram:GuidelineSpecifiedDocumentContextParameter>
  </rsm:ExchangedDocumentContext>

  <rsm:ExchangedDocument>
    <ram:ID>INV-001</ram:ID>
    <ram:TypeCode>380</ram:TypeCode>
    <ram:IssueDateTime>
      <udt:DateTimeString format="102">20250101</udt:DateTimeString>
    </ram:IssueDateTime>
  </rsm:ExchangedDocument>

  <rsm:SupplyChainTradeTransaction>

    <ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeAgreement>
      <ram:BuyerReference>Buyer</ram:BuyerReference>

      <ram:SellerTradeParty>
        <ram:Name>My Test Company</ram:Name>
        <ram:SpecifiedLegalOrganization>

          <ram:CountryID>FR</ram:CountryID>

    <ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeSettlement>
      <ram:InvoiceCurrencyCode>EUR</ram:InvoiceCurrencyCode>

Step 2 — Create facturx_engine.py
In VS Code: Right‑click your main folder FACTURX_PROJECT → New File → name it: ✅ facturx_engine.py Paste this code:
import os
import tempfile
from facturx import generate_from_file


def embed_facturx(pdf_bytes: bytes, xml_bytes: bytes) -> bytes:
    """
    Takes:
      - original PDF bytes
      - Factur-X XML bytes
    Returns:
      - Factur-X PDF bytes
    """

    # Windows needs delete=False, then we close and delete manually
    pdf_tmp = tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".pdf", delete=False)
    xml_tmp = tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".xml", delete=False)
    out_tmp = tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".pdf", delete=False)

    try:
        pdf_tmp.write(pdf_bytes)
        pdf_tmp.close()

        xml_tmp.write(xml_bytes)
        xml_tmp.close()

        out_tmp.close()

        generate_from_file(pdf_tmp.name, xml_tmp.name, output_pdf_file=out_tmp.name)

        with open(out_tmp.name, "rb") as f:
            return f.read()

    finally:
        for path in [pdf_tmp.name, xml_tmp.name, out_tmp.name]:
            try:
                os.remove(path)
            except OSError:
                pass
Step 3 — Create facturx_xml.py (XML generator)
Right‑click FACTURX_PROJECT → New File → name it: ✅ facturx_xml.py Paste this code:
from datetime import date
from decimal import Decimal, ROUND_HALF_UP
from xml.sax.saxutils import escape


def _money(x: Decimal) -> str:
    # Always 2 decimals, with dot
    return str(x.quantize(Decimal("0.01"), rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP))


def build_facturx_minimum_xml(
    invoice_number: str,
    invoice_date: date,
    seller_name: str,
    seller_siret: str,
    seller_vat: str,
    buyer_name: str,
    total_ht: Decimal,
    vat_rate_percent: Decimal,
    currency: str = "EUR",
) -> bytes:
    """
    Simple Factur-X MINIMUM builder for learning:
    - One VAT rate only
    - Totals: HT, VAT, TTC
    """

    # Compute VAT and TTC
    vat_amount = (total_ht * vat_rate_percent / Decimal("100")).quantize(Decimal("0.01"), rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP)
    total_ttc = (total_ht + vat_amount).quantize(Decimal("0.01"), rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP)

    # Date format required: YYYYMMDD
    yyyymmdd = invoice_date.strftime("%Y%m%d")

    # Escape names for XML safety
    seller_name = escape(seller_name)
    buyer_name = escape(buyer_name)
    invoice_number = escape(invoice_number)

    xml = f"""<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<rsm:CrossIndustryInvoice
  xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
  xmlns:qdt="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:QualifiedDataType:100"
  xmlns:udt="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:UnqualifiedDataType:100"
  xmlns:rsm="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:CrossIndustryInvoice:100"
  xmlns:ram="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:ReusableAggregateBusinessInformationEntity:100">

  <rsm:ExchangedDocumentContext>
    <ram:GuidelineSpecifiedDocumentContextParameter>
      <ram:ID>urn:factur-x.eu:1p0:minimum</ram:ID>
    </ram:GuidelineSpecifiedDocumentContextParameter>
  </rsm:ExchangedDocumentContext>

  <rsm:ExchangedDocument>
    <ram:ID>{invoice_number}</ram:ID>
    <ram:TypeCode>380</ram:TypeCode>
    <ram:IssueDateTime>
      <udt:DateTimeString format="102">{yyyymmdd}</udt:DateTimeString>
    </ram:IssueDateTime>
  </rsm:ExchangedDocument>

  <rsm:SupplyChainTradeTransaction>

    <ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeAgreement>

      <ram:SellerTradeParty>
        <ram:Name>{seller_name}</ram:Name>
        <ram:SpecifiedLegalOrganization>
          <ram:ID schemeID="0002">{escape(seller_siret)}</ram:ID>
        </ram:SpecifiedLegalOrganization>
        <ram:SpecifiedTaxRegistration>
          <ram:ID schemeID="VA">{escape(seller_vat)}</ram:ID>
        </ram:SpecifiedTaxRegistration>
      </ram:SellerTradeParty>

      <ram:BuyerTradeParty>
        <ram:Name>{buyer_name}</ram:Name>
      </ram:BuyerTradeParty>

    </ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeAgreement>

    <ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeDelivery/>

    <ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeSettlement>
      <ram:InvoiceCurrencyCode>{currency}</ram:InvoiceCurrencyCode>

      <ram:ApplicableTradeTax>
        <ram:CalculatedAmount currencyID="{currency}">{_money(vat_amount)}</ram:CalculatedAmount>
        <ram:TypeCode>VAT</ram:TypeCode>
        <ram:BasisAmount currencyID="{currency}">{_money(total_ht)}</ram:BasisAmount>
        <ram:CategoryCode>S</ram:CategoryCode>
        <ram:RateApplicablePercent>{_money(vat_rate_percent)}</ram:RateApplicablePercent>
      </ram:ApplicableTradeTax>

      <ram:SpecifiedTradeSettlementHeaderMonetarySummation>
        <ram:TaxBasisTotalAmount>{_money(total_ht)}</ram:TaxBasisTotalAmount>
        <ram:TaxTotalAmount currencyID="{currency}">{_money(vat_amount)}</ram:TaxTotalAmount>
        <ram:GrandTotalAmount>{_money(total_ttc)}</ram:GrandTotalAmount>
        <ram:DuePayableAmount>{_money(total_ttc)}</ram:DuePayableAmount>
      </ram:SpecifiedTradeSettlementHeaderMonetarySummation>

    </ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeSettlement>

  </rsm:SupplyChainTradeTransaction>
</rsm:CrossIndustryInvoice>
"""
    return xml.encode("utf-8")
Important (so you understand):
This builder is a learning / simple “Minimum profile” generator:
It assumes one VAT rate only.
Real invoices can have multiple VAT rates, line items, discounts, etc.
We’ll add those later.
Step 4 — Create app.py (the mini website)
Right‑click FACTURX_PROJECT → New File → name it: ✅ app.py Paste this code:
import streamlit as st
from datetime import date
from decimal import Decimal, InvalidOperation

from facturx_engine import embed_facturx
from facturx_xml import build_facturx_minimum_xml


st.set_page_config(page_title="Factur-X Converter", layout="centered")
st.title("Factur‑X Converter (Local Demo)")

uploaded_pdf = st.file_uploader("Upload your invoice PDF", type=["pdf"])

st.subheader("Invoice details")

invoice_number = st.text_input("Invoice Number", value="INV-001")
invoice_date = st.date_input("Invoice Date", value=date.today())

st.subheader("Seller (your company)")
seller_name = st.text_input("Seller Name", value="My Company")
seller_siret = st.text_input("Seller SIRET", value="12345678900011")
seller_vat = st.text_input("Seller VAT (FR...)", value="FR11123456789")

st.subheader("Buyer (your customer)")
buyer_name = st.text_input("Buyer Name", value="Customer Name")

st.subheader("Amounts")
total_ht_str = st.text_input("Total HT (ex: 100.00)", value="100.00")
vat_rate_str = st.text_input("VAT rate % (ex: 20)", value="20")

if uploaded_pdf:
    if st.button("Generate Factur‑X PDF"):
        try:
            total_ht = Decimal(total_ht_str.replace(",", "."))
            vat_rate_percent = Decimal(vat_rate_str.replace(",", "."))
        except InvalidOperation:
            st.error("Amounts not valid. Use numbers like 100.00 and 20")
            st.stop()

        xml_bytes = build_facturx_minimum_xml(
            invoice_number=invoice_number,
            invoice_date=invoice_date,
            seller_name=seller_name,
            seller_siret=seller_siret,
            seller_vat=seller_vat,
            buyer_name=buyer_name,
            total_ht=total_ht,
            vat_rate_percent=vat_rate_percent,
        )

        pdf_bytes = uploaded_pdf.read()
        out_bytes = embed_facturx(pdf_bytes, xml_bytes)

        st.success("Done! Download your Factur‑X PDF below:")
        st.download_button(
            "Download Factur‑X PDF",
            data=out_bytes,
            file_name=f"{invoice_number}_facturx.pdf",
            mime="application/pdf",
        )
else:
    st.info("Upload a PDF to enable generation.")

import os
import tempfile
from pathlib import Path

import streamlit as st
from facturx import generate_from_file


st.set_page_config(page_title="Factur‑X Converter (Local)", layout="centered")
st.title("Factur‑X Converter (Local)")
st.write("Upload a PDF → download a Factur‑X PDF (XML embedded).")

# We will reuse your already-working Factur‑X XML file for now
BASE_DIR = Path(__file__).parent
XML_PATH = BASE_DIR / "input" / "sample_invoice.xml"

if not XML_PATH.exists():
    st.error("❌ Missing file: input/sample_invoice.xml")
    st.stop()

uploaded_pdf = st.file_uploader("Upload your invoice PDF", type=["pdf"])

if uploaded_pdf is not None:
    st.info("✅ PDF uploaded. Click convert to generate the Factur‑X PDF.")

    if st.button("Convert to Factur‑X"):
        # 1) Save uploaded PDF to a temporary file
        with tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(delete=False, suffix=".pdf") as tmp_pdf:
            tmp_pdf.write(uploaded_pdf.getbuffer())
            pdf_path = tmp_pdf.name

        # 2) Create a temporary output file path
        out_fd, out_path = tempfile.mkstemp(suffix=".pdf")
        os.close(out_fd)

        try:
            # 3) Convert (embed XML into PDF)
            generate_from_file(
                pdf_path,
                str(XML_PATH),
                output_pdf_file=out_path,
            )

            # 4) Read result as bytes so Streamlit can offer download
            with open(out_path, "rb") as f:
                facturx_bytes = f.read()

            st.success("✅ Done! Your Factur‑X PDF is ready.")
            st.download_button(
                "Download Factur‑X PDF",
                data=facturx_bytes,
                file_name="facturx_invoice.pdf",
                mime="application/pdf",
            )

        finally:
            # Cleanup temp files
            try:
                os.remove(pdf_path)
            except OSError:
                pass
            try:
                os.remove(out_path)
            except OSError:
                pass
Save the file: CTRL + S

You should see something like:

Make the XML “dynamic” (you type invoice number/date/total in the UI, and we generate the XML with those values).

Step 3A — Create one new file: facturx_xml.py
In VS Code (left sidebar):

Right-click FACTURX_PROJECT → New File

Name it:

facturx_xml.py

Paste this code and save (Ctrl+S):

from datetime import date
from decimal import Decimal, ROUND_HALF_UP
from xml.sax.saxutils import escape


def _money(x: Decimal) -> str:
    return str(x.quantize(Decimal("0.01"), rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP))


def build_facturx_minimum_xml(
    invoice_number: str,
    invoice_date: date,
    seller_name: str,
    buyer_name: str,
    total_ht: Decimal,
    vat_rate_percent: Decimal,
    currency: str = "EUR",
) -> bytes:
    vat_amount = (total_ht * vat_rate_percent / Decimal("100")).quantize(
        Decimal("0.01"), rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP
    )
    total_ttc = (total_ht + vat_amount).quantize(Decimal("0.01"), rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP)

    yyyymmdd = invoice_date.strftime("%Y%m%d")

    xml = f"""<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<rsm:CrossIndustryInvoice
  xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
  xmlns:qdt="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:QualifiedDataType:100"
  xmlns:udt="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:UnqualifiedDataType:100"
  xmlns:rsm="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:CrossIndustryInvoice:100"
  xmlns:ram="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:ReusableAggregateBusinessInformationEntity:100">

  <rsm:ExchangedDocumentContext>
    <ram:GuidelineSpecifiedDocumentContextParameter>
      <ram:ID>urn:factur-x.eu:1p0:minimum</ram:ID>
    </ram:GuidelineSpecifiedDocumentContextParameter>
  </rsm:ExchangedDocumentContext>

  <rsm:ExchangedDocument>
    <ram:ID>{escape(invoice_number)}</ram:ID>
    <ram:TypeCode>380</ram:TypeCode>
    <ram:IssueDateTime>
      <udt:DateTimeString format="102">{yyyymmdd}</udt:DateTimeString>
    </ram:IssueDateTime>
  </rsm:ExchangedDocument>

  <rsm:SupplyChainTradeTransaction>
    <ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeAgreement>
      <ram:SellerTradeParty>
        <ram:Name>{escape(seller_name)}</ram:Name>
      </ram:SellerTradeParty>
      <ram:BuyerTradeParty>
        <ram:Name>{escape(buyer_name)}</ram:Name>
      </ram:BuyerTradeParty>
    </ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeAgreement>

    <ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeDelivery/>

    <ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeSettlement>
      <ram:InvoiceCurrencyCode>{currency}</ram:InvoiceCurrencyCode>

      <ram:ApplicableTradeTax>
        <ram:CalculatedAmount currencyID="{currency}">{_money(vat_amount)}</ram:CalculatedAmount>
        <ram:TypeCode>VAT</ram:TypeCode>
        <ram:BasisAmount currencyID="{currency}">{_money(total_ht)}</ram:BasisAmount>
        <ram:CategoryCode>S</ram:CategoryCode>
        <ram:RateApplicablePercent>{_money(vat_rate_percent)}</ram:RateApplicablePercent>
      </ram:ApplicableTradeTax>

      <ram:SpecifiedTradeSettlementHeaderMonetarySummation>
        <ram:TaxBasisTotalAmount>{_money(total_ht)}</ram:TaxBasisTotalAmount>
        <ram:TaxTotalAmount currencyID="{currency}">{_money(vat_amount)}</ram:TaxTotalAmount>
        <ram:GrandTotalAmount>{_money(total_ttc)}</ram:GrandTotalAmount>
        <ram:DuePayableAmount>{_money(total_ttc)}</ram:DuePayableAmount>
      </ram:SpecifiedTradeSettlementHeaderMonetarySummation>

    </ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeSettlement>
  </rsm:SupplyChainTradeTransaction>
</rsm:CrossIndustryInvoice>
"""
    return xml.encode("utf-8")

            total_ht = Decimal(total_ht_str.replace(",", "."))

        st.success("Done! Download your Factur‑X PDF below:")
        st.download_button(
            "Download Factur‑X PDF",
            data=out_bytes,
            file_name=f"{invoice_number}_facturx.pdf",

What this error means (10-year-old version)
Factur-X XML is like a very strict recipe.

Your XML has the right “ingredients” (VAT, totals…), but they are in the wrong order.

The library is saying:

“I expected to see the Totals block first, but I saw the Tax block first.”

So we just need to swap the order of two blocks inside facturx_xml.py.

✅ Fix (1 step): Move the VAT block below the Totals block
Step 1 — Open facturx_xml.py

<ram:SpecifiedTradeSettlementHeaderMonetarySummation> ... </ram:SpecifiedTradeSettlementHeaderMonetarySummation> ✅ (Totals block)

Step 3 — Make sure the order is like this (Totals FIRST, VAT AFTER)
✅ Correct order should be:

<ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeSettlement>
  <ram:InvoiceCurrencyCode>EUR</ram:InvoiceCurrencyCode>

  <ram:SpecifiedTradeSettlementHeaderMonetarySummation>
    ...
  </ram:SpecifiedTradeSettlementHeaderMonetarySummation>

  <ram:ApplicableTradeTax>
    ...
  </ram:ApplicableTradeTax>

</ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeSettlement>
So: cut the whole <ram:ApplicableTradeTax> ... </ram:ApplicableTradeTax> block
and paste it below the <ram:SpecifiedTradeSettlementHeaderMonetarySummation> ... block.

✅ Step: Replace your entire facturx_xml.py with this
Open facturx_xml.py in VS Code

from datetime import date
from decimal import Decimal, ROUND_HALF_UP
from xml.sax.saxutils import escape


def _money(x: Decimal) -> str:
    return str(x.quantize(Decimal("0.01"), rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP))


def build_facturx_minimum_xml(
    invoice_number: str,
    invoice_date: date,
    seller_name: str,
    seller_siret: str,
    seller_vat: str,
    buyer_name: str,
    total_ht: Decimal,
    vat_rate_percent: Decimal,
    currency: str = "EUR",
) -> bytes:
    """
    Factur-X MINIMUM profile XML (simple version).
    IMPORTANT: MINIMUM profile is very strict and does NOT accept some blocks
    like ApplicableTradeTax in our previous version.

    We still compute VAT and totals, but we only output the totals section
    (MonetarySummation), which is acceptable for MINIMUM.
    """

    # Calculate VAT and TTC (rounded to 2 decimals)
    vat_amount = (total_ht * vat_rate_percent / Decimal("100")).quantize(
        Decimal("0.01"), rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP
    )
    total_ttc = (total_ht + vat_amount).quantize(Decimal("0.01"), rounding=ROUND_HALF_UP)

    # Date format needed in XML: YYYYMMDD
    yyyymmdd = invoice_date.strftime("%Y%m%d")

    xml = f"""<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<rsm:CrossIndustryInvoice
  xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
  xmlns:qdt="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:QualifiedDataType:100"
  xmlns:udt="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:UnqualifiedDataType:100"
  xmlns:rsm="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:CrossIndustryInvoice:100"
  xmlns:ram="urn:un:unece:uncefact:data:standard:ReusableAggregateBusinessInformationEntity:100">

  <rsm:ExchangedDocumentContext>
    <ram:GuidelineSpecifiedDocumentContextParameter>
      <ram:ID>urn:factur-x.eu:1p0:minimum</ram:ID>
    </ram:GuidelineSpecifiedDocumentContextParameter>
  </rsm:ExchangedDocumentContext>

  <rsm:ExchangedDocument>
    <ram:ID>{escape(invoice_number)}</ram:ID>
    <ram:TypeCode>380</ram:TypeCode>
    <ram:IssueDateTime>
      <udt:DateTimeString format="102">{yyyymmdd}</udt:DateTimeString>
    </ram:IssueDateTime>
  </rsm:ExchangedDocument>

  <rsm:SupplyChainTradeTransaction>

    <ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeAgreement>

      <ram:SellerTradeParty>
        <ram:Name>{escape(seller_name)}</ram:Name>

        <ram:SpecifiedLegalOrganization>
          <ram:ID schemeID="0002">{escape(seller_siret)}</ram:ID>
        </ram:SpecifiedLegalOrganization>

        <ram:SpecifiedTaxRegistration>
          <ram:ID schemeID="VA">{escape(seller_vat)}</ram:ID>
        </ram:SpecifiedTaxRegistration>
      </ram:SellerTradeParty>

      <ram:BuyerTradeParty>
        <ram:Name>{escape(buyer_name)}</ram:Name>
      </ram:BuyerTradeParty>

    </ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeAgreement>

    <ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeDelivery/>

    <ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeSettlement>
      <ram:InvoiceCurrencyCode>{currency}</ram:InvoiceCurrencyCode>

      <ram:SpecifiedTradeSettlementHeaderMonetarySummation>
        <ram:TaxBasisTotalAmount>{_money(total_ht)}</ram:TaxBasisTotalAmount>
        <ram:TaxTotalAmount currencyID="{currency}">{_money(vat_amount)}</ram:TaxTotalAmount>
        <ram:GrandTotalAmount>{_money(total_ttc)}</ram:GrandTotalAmount>
        <ram:DuePayableAmount>{_money(total_ttc)}</ram:DuePayableAmount>
      </ram:SpecifiedTradeSettlementHeaderMonetarySummation>

    </ram:ApplicableHeaderTradeSettlement>

  </rsm:SupplyChainTradeTransaction>
</rsm:CrossIndustryInvoice>
"""
    return xml.encode("utf-8")

ChatGPT said:

Thought for 16s
Yep — that’s exactly how it should look. ✅

Why it looks the same
Factur-X is a normal PDF that humans read (the page you see) plus a hidden XML file for computers inside the PDF.

So the visual PDF you uploaded should look basically unchanged after conversion — that’s the whole point of Factur-X: humans see the same invoice, robots get the data.

Your screenshot invoice (Zomato/Eternal) is just the “human view,” and that’s fine. 
sample_invoice


One quick check to be 100% sure it’s really Factur-X
In your terminal (with (venv)), run:

facturx-pdfextractxml output\sample_invoice_facturx.pdf output\check.xml
If it generates output\check.xml and you can open it and see <rsm:CrossIndustryInvoice ...>, then ✅ it’s a proper Factur-X file.

(You already did this once, so you’re basically confirmed.)

Important note (so you don’t get surprised later)
Right now, your app creates Factur-X XML using the fields you type (invoice number/date/totals etc). That means:

The PDF looks like Zomato invoice

But the embedded XML contains whatever values you typed (like your test seller/buyer names)

So visually it’s fine, but legally, in the future we must make sure the XML matches the PDF (that’s where OCR automation comes in).

If you want the next step (slow, one step):
✅ Step 4 = automatically read invoice number + date + totals from the PDF (OCR), and auto-fill your form.

INV-001_facturx

In VS Code → right-click FACTURX_PROJECT → New File → name it:

pdf_autofill.py

Now copy-paste this whole code:

import io
import re
from datetime import datetime, date
from typing import Optional, Dict, Any

from pypdf import PdfReader


def _extract_text(pdf_bytes: bytes) -> str:
    reader = PdfReader(io.BytesIO(pdf_bytes))
    parts = []
    for page in reader.pages:
        t = page.extract_text() or ""
        parts.append(t)
    return "\n".join(parts)


def _parse_date(s: str) -> Optional[date]:
    s = s.strip()

    # YYYY-MM-DD
    m = re.search(r"(\d{4})-(\d{2})-(\d{2})", s)
    if m:
        y, mo, d = map(int, m.groups())
        return date(y, mo, d)

    # DD/MM/YYYY
    m = re.search(r"(\d{2})/(\d{2})/(\d{4})", s)
    if m:
        d, mo, y = map(int, m.groups())
        return date(y, mo, d)

    return None


def extract_fields(pdf_bytes: bytes) -> Dict[str, Any]:
    """
    Tries to extract basic fields from a text-based PDF.
    Works best when the PDF has selectable text (not scanned images).
    """
    text = _extract_text(pdf_bytes)

    out: Dict[str, Any] = {}

    # Invoice number + date (matches your Zomato-style invoice too)
    m = re.search(
        r"Invoice\s*No:\s*([A-Z0-9\-]+)\s+Invoice\s*Date:\s*([0-9]{4}-[0-9]{2}-[0-9]{2})",
        text,
        flags=re.IGNORECASE,
    )
    if m:
        out["invoice_number"] = m.group(1).strip()
        out["invoice_date"] = _parse_date(m.group(2)) or date.today()

    # Try to find a "Total ... 10.00 0.90 0.90 11.80" line:
    # - total_ht = first number after the word Total
    # - total_ttc = last number on that line
    total_line = None
    for line in text.splitlines():
        if re.search(r"\bTotal\b", line):
            nums = re.findall(r"(\d+\.\d{2})", line)
            if len(nums) >= 2:
                total_line = line
                total_ht = nums[0]
                total_ttc = nums[-1]
                out["total_ht_str"] = total_ht
                out["total_ttc_str"] = total_ttc
                break

    return out
4B) Replace your entire app.py with this (copy-paste)
Open app.py → Ctrl+A → Delete → paste everything below → Ctrl+S

import streamlit as st
from datetime import date
from decimal import Decimal, InvalidOperation

from facturx_engine import embed_facturx
from facturx_xml import build_facturx_minimum_xml
from pdf_autofill import extract_fields


st.set_page_config(page_title="Factur-X Converter", layout="centered")
st.title("Factur-X Converter (Local Demo)")

uploaded_pdf = st.file_uploader("Upload your invoice PDF", type=["pdf"])

# --- Session defaults (so inputs have values) ---
if "invoice_number" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.invoice_number = "INV-001"
if "invoice_date" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.invoice_date = date.today()
if "seller_name" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.seller_name = "My Company"
if "seller_siret" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.seller_siret = "12345678900011"
if "seller_vat" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.seller_vat = "FR11123456789"
if "buyer_name" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.buyer_name = "Customer Name"
if "total_ht_str" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.total_ht_str = "100.00"
if "vat_rate_str" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.vat_rate_str = "20"

# --- Auto-fill button ---
if uploaded_pdf is not None:
    if st.button("Auto-fill from PDF"):
        fields = extract_fields(uploaded_pdf.read())

        # Put extracted fields into the form
        for k, v in fields.items():
            if v is None:
                continue
            st.session_state[k] = v

        st.success("Auto-fill done (if the PDF had selectable text). Re-check the fields below.")

# --- Form inputs ---
st.subheader("Invoice details")
invoice_number = st.text_input("Invoice Number", key="invoice_number")
invoice_date = st.date_input("Invoice Date", key="invoice_date")

st.subheader("Seller (your company)")
seller_name = st.text_input("Seller Name", key="seller_name")
seller_siret = st.text_input("Seller SIRET", key="seller_siret")
seller_vat = st.text_input("Seller VAT (FR...)", key="seller_vat")

st.subheader("Buyer (your customer)")
buyer_name = st.text_input("Buyer Name", key="buyer_name")

st.subheader("Amounts")
total_ht_str = st.text_input("Total HT (ex: 100.00)", key="total_ht_str")
vat_rate_str = st.text_input("VAT rate % (ex: 20)", key="vat_rate_str")

# --- Generate ---
if uploaded_pdf:
    if st.button("Generate Factur-X PDF"):
        try:
            total_ht = Decimal(str(total_ht_str).replace(",", "."))
            vat_rate_percent = Decimal(str(vat_rate_str).replace(",", "."))
        except InvalidOperation:
            st.error("Amounts not valid. Use numbers like 100.00 and 20")
            st.stop()

        xml_bytes = build_facturx_minimum_xml(
            invoice_number=invoice_number,
            invoice_date=invoice_date,
            seller_name=seller_name,
            seller_siret=seller_siret,
            seller_vat=seller_vat,
            buyer_name=buyer_name,
            total_ht=total_ht,
            vat_rate_percent=vat_rate_percent,
        )

        # IMPORTANT: because we already read the PDF once for auto-fill,
        # we need to re-read it fresh here.
        uploaded_pdf.seek(0)
        pdf_bytes = uploaded_pdf.read()

        out_bytes = embed_facturx(pdf_bytes, xml_bytes)

        st.success("Done! Download your Factur-X PDF below:")
        st.download_button(
            "Download Factur-X PDF",
            data=out_bytes,
            file_name=f"{invoice_number}_facturx.pdf",
            mime="application/pdf",
        )
else:
    st.info("Upload a PDF to enable generation.")

Step 5 (one step): Add a “Trust Check” before download (validation)
Right now the app generates a file. Next we add a validator so it says:

✅ “This Factur-X XML is valid (minimum profile)”
or
❌ “Invalid — fix these fields”

5A) Create a new file: validator.py
Create validator.py in the main folder and paste this:

from facturx import xml_check_xsd

def validate_facturx_minimum(xml_bytes: bytes) -> None:
    """
    Raises an Exception if XML is not valid for Factur-X MINIMUM.
    If no error, it is valid.
    """
    xml_check_xsd(xml_bytes, flavor="factur-x", level="minimum")
5B) Update app.py (copy-paste just these 2 edits)
1) Add this import at the top:
from validator import validate_facturx_minimum
2) Right after you build xml_bytes = build_facturx_minimum_xml(...), add this:
try:
    validate_facturx_minimum(xml_bytes)
    st.success("✅ XML validated (Factur-X MINIMUM)")
except Exception as e:
    st.error("❌ XML is NOT valid. Fix fields before generating.")
    st.code(str(e))
    st.stop()

from facturx import xml_check_xsd


def validate_facturx_minimum(xml_bytes: bytes) -> None:
    """
    If XML is valid, this returns normally.
    If XML is invalid, it raises an exception.
    """
    xml_check_xsd(xml_bytes, flavor="factur-x", level="minimum")
✅ Step 5B — Replace your WHOLE app.py with this (copy/paste)
Open app.py → Ctrl+A → Delete → paste below → Ctrl+S

import streamlit as st
from datetime import date
from decimal import Decimal, InvalidOperation

from facturx_engine import embed_facturx
from facturx_xml import build_facturx_minimum_xml
from pdf_autofill import extract_fields
from validator import validate_facturx_minimum


st.set_page_config(page_title="Factur-X Converter", layout="centered")
st.title("Factur-X Converter (Local Demo)")

uploaded_pdf = st.file_uploader("Upload your invoice PDF", type=["pdf"])

# -------------------------
# Session defaults
# -------------------------
if "invoice_number" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.invoice_number = "INV-001"
if "invoice_date" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.invoice_date = date.today()
if "seller_name" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.seller_name = "My Company"
if "seller_siret" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.seller_siret = "12345678900011"
if "seller_vat" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.seller_vat = "FR11123456789"
if "buyer_name" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.buyer_name = "Customer Name"
if "total_ht_str" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.total_ht_str = "100.00"
if "vat_rate_str" not in st.session_state:
    st.session_state.vat_rate_str = "20"

# -------------------------
# Auto-fill button
# -------------------------
if uploaded_pdf is not None:
    if st.button("Auto-fill from PDF"):
        pdf_bytes_for_autofill = uploaded_pdf.read()
        fields = extract_fields(pdf_bytes_for_autofill)

        for k, v in fields.items():
            if v is None:
                continue
            st.session_state[k] = v

        st.success("Auto-fill done. Re-check fields below.")

# -------------------------
# Form inputs
# -------------------------
st.subheader("Invoice details")
invoice_number = st.text_input("Invoice Number", key="invoice_number")
invoice_date = st.date_input("Invoice Date", key="invoice_date")

st.subheader("Seller (your company)")
seller_name = st.text_input("Seller Name", key="seller_name")
seller_siret = st.text_input("Seller SIRET", key="seller_siret")
seller_vat = st.text_input("Seller VAT (FR...)", key="seller_vat")

st.subheader("Buyer (your customer)")
buyer_name = st.text_input("Buyer Name", key="buyer_name")

st.subheader("Amounts")
total_ht_str = st.text_input("Total HT (ex: 100.00)", key="total_ht_str")
vat_rate_str = st.text_input("VAT rate % (ex: 20)", key="vat_rate_str")

# -------------------------
# Generate
# -------------------------
if uploaded_pdf:
    if st.button("Generate Factur-X PDF"):
        # 1) Parse numbers safely
        try:
            total_ht = Decimal(str(total_ht_str).replace(",", "."))
            vat_rate_percent = Decimal(str(vat_rate_str).replace(",", "."))
        except InvalidOperation:
            st.error("Amounts not valid. Use numbers like 100.00 and 20")
            st.stop()

        # 2) Build XML
        xml_bytes = build_facturx_minimum_xml(
            invoice_number=invoice_number,
            invoice_date=invoice_date,
            seller_name=seller_name,
            seller_siret=seller_siret,
            seller_vat=seller_vat,
            buyer_name=buyer_name,
            total_ht=total_ht,
            vat_rate_percent=vat_rate_percent,
        )

        # 3) Validate XML BEFORE generating PDF
        try:
            validate_facturx_minimum(xml_bytes)
            st.success("✅ XML validated (Factur-X MINIMUM)")
        except Exception as e:
            st.error("❌ XML is NOT valid. Fix fields before generating.")
            st.code(str(e))
            st.stop()

        # 4) Re-read PDF bytes (important)
        uploaded_pdf.seek(0)
        pdf_bytes = uploaded_pdf.read()

        # 5) Embed XML into PDF
        out_bytes = embed_facturx(pdf_bytes, xml_bytes)

        st.success("✅ Done! Download your Factur-X PDF below:")
        st.download_button(
            "Download Factur-X PDF",
            data=out_bytes,
            file_name=f"{invoice_number}_facturx.pdf",
            mime="application/pdf",
        )
else:
    st.info("Upload a PDF to enable generation.")

✅ Yes — “Validation success” means your generated file does contain an embedded XML and that XML is valid Factur-X MINIMUM according to the official schema check (the library is basically saying “the XML shape is correct”).

Does your PDF now have “the XML file the government needs”?
Technically: yes, it has a Factur-X XML embedded.
Legally/for production in France: not yet guaranteed, for 2 reasons:

Your PDF content is not a French B2B invoice (your sample is an Indian GST invoice from Zomato/Eternal — you can see GSTIN/PAN, etc. 
Z26MHOT025818768_facturx (2)

). France expects SIRET/VAT rules, French seller/buyer identifiers, etc.

Even if the XML is valid “Factur-X MINIMUM”, French platforms can still reject invoices if:

required French business data is missing (SIRET/SIREN, addresses, VAT breakdown rules, etc.)

the XML values don’t match what the PDF shows

you need a higher profile (often BASIC WL or EN16931) depending on use case

So: you’ve built a correct Factur-X container. The next work is making the data inside match real French requirements + real invoice content.

Yep — that’s normal, and it’s actually an important concept:

Why the name didn’t change in the downloaded PDF
Your converter is doing this:

It takes the original PDF (the “picture humans see”) and keeps it unchanged.

It adds a hidden XML inside it (the “data computers read”).

So the visible name on the page will stay “Sudeep Daggaonkar …” because that text is part of the original invoice PDF from Privé by Zalando. 
INV-001_facturx (2)


Changing the visible PDF text would be a different product (PDF editor) and would risk breaking layouts, fonts, and legal invoice appearance. Factur-X is designed specifically so the visual PDF stays the same.

What should change (and what matters)
The thing that should match your form fields is the embedded XML inside the PDF — not the visible page.

Quick proof (1 command)

facturx-pdfextractxml "INV-001_facturx (2).pdf" output\check.xml
Open output\check.xml and you’ll see the values your app generated (invoice number, buyer name, totals, etc.).
That’s the “government/computer” part.

Important note for your France project
Your screenshot invoice is a consumer invoice (Privé by Zalando) — it even says it’s for personal use and not for VAT deduction. 
INV-001_facturx (2)

Yes — that’s basically the right idea, with one important correction:

What “Azure free version” really means
Azure Document Intelligence has a free tier (F0) that’s meant for testing and early prototypes. It has hard limits (quota + restrictions). For example, people commonly hit limits like:

only the first 2 pages analyzed per request on F0 
Microsoft Learn
+1

monthly page/call quota limits (you’ll start getting “out of call volume quota” errors once you hit the free quota) 
Microsoft Learn

So yes: for starting / testing it’s perfect. But once you have real usage, you’ll need paid (S0 / pay-as-you-go).

It’s not about “10–20 customers”
It’s about how many pages you process per month.

If you have 10 customers but they convert lots of invoices (many pages), you’ll hit limits fast.

If you have 50 customers but they rarely convert, you might stay within free tier longer.

Azure billing is per page processed in general. 
Microsoft Azure
+1

What you should do for your project (best plan)
✅ Now (MVP): Use your current flow + add Azure OCR on F0 to test
✅ When launching: Switch to paid tier and charge users accordingly (freemium limits, then paid)

✅ Step 4A: Make Azure read the invoice and print the extracted fields (test first)
1) Install 2 libraries (copy-paste in VS Code terminal)

2) Create a file named .env in your project folder (same place as app.py)

DOCUMENTINTELLIGENCE_ENDPOINT="https://YOUR-RESOURCE-NAME.cognitiveservices.azure.com/"

3) Replace your pdf_autofill.py with this full code (copy-paste everything)
Create/overwrite pdf_autofill.py:

import os
import sys
import io
from dotenv import load_dotenv
from azure.core.credentials import AzureKeyCredential
from azure.ai.documentintelligence import DocumentIntelligenceClient


def extract_invoice_fields(pdf_bytes: bytes) -> dict:
    load_dotenv()

    endpoint = os.getenv("DOCUMENTINTELLIGENCE_ENDPOINT")
    key = os.getenv("DOCUMENTINTELLIGENCE_API_KEY")

    if not endpoint or not key:
        raise RuntimeError(
            "Missing DOCUMENTINTELLIGENCE_ENDPOINT or DOCUMENTINTELLIGENCE_API_KEY in your .env file"
        )

    client = DocumentIntelligenceClient(
        endpoint=endpoint,
        credential=AzureKeyCredential(key),
    )

    poller = client.begin_analyze_document(
        "prebuilt-invoice",
        body=io.BytesIO(pdf_bytes),
    )
    result = poller.result()

    if not result.documents:
        return {}

    doc = result.documents[0]
    fields = doc.fields or {}

    def get_string(field_name: str):
        f = fields.get(field_name)
        if not f:
            return None
        return f.get("valueString") or f.get("content")

    def get_date(field_name: str):
        f = fields.get(field_name)
        if not f:
            return None
        return f.get("valueDate") or f.get("content")

    def get_currency_amount(field_name: str):
        f = fields.get(field_name)
        if not f:
            return None
        cur = f.get("valueCurrency")
        if isinstance(cur, dict):
            return cur.get("amount")
        return None

    return {
        "invoice_number": get_string("InvoiceId") or get_string("InvoiceNumber"),
        "invoice_date": get_date("InvoiceDate"),
        "seller_name": get_string("VendorName"),
        "buyer_name": get_string("CustomerName"),
        "invoice_total": get_currency_amount("InvoiceTotal") or get_currency_amount("AmountDue"),
    }


if __name__ == "__main__":
    if len(sys.argv) < 2:
        print("Usage: python pdf_autofill.py path\\to\\invoice.pdf")
        sys.exit(1)

    pdf_path = sys.argv[1]

    with open(pdf_path, "rb") as f:
        pdf_bytes = f.read()

    data = extract_invoice_fields(pdf_bytes)
    print("\n✅ Extracted fields from Azure:")
    for k, v in data.items():
        print(f"- {k}: {v}")

Totally fair — “create a .env file” sounds weird until you see it once. Here’s what it means in super simple terms.

What is a .env file?
It’s just a plain text file where we store secret settings like:

your Azure endpoint (a URL)

your Azure API key (a secret password)

We put them in a .env file so:

you don’t paste secrets into your code

you can share your code later without leaking your key

Step 4A-2 — Exactly what to do (VS Code)

Not env, not .env.txt.

What the error is saying (in simple words)
You are logged in with a Microsoft account, but Azure Portal is trying to open in a tenant (directory) called “Microsoft Services”, and your account is NOT allowed inside that tenant.

That’s why it says things like:

“User account … does not exist in tenant ‘Microsoft Services’”

“cannot access the application Azure Portal in that tenant”

“Sign out and sign in again with a different Azure Active Directory user account”

So this is not a coding issue. It’s an Azure login / tenant access issue.

✅ Fix it (do these steps exactly)
Step 1 — Click Sign in again
On that popup, click Sign in again (not Ignore).

Step 2 — Use the correct login method
When it asks for account:

Choose your personal Microsoft account (the one you want to use for Azure)

If it shows multiple accounts, pick the one that will own the subscription.

If you’re unsure, the easiest safe way is:

✅ Use a clean browser session
Open an Incognito / InPrivate window

Go to Azure Portal

Sign in with only one account

This avoids Azure mixing accounts/tenants.

✅ Step 3 — Force Azure to open in the “common” tenant
Sometimes Azure gets stuck in the wrong tenant. The safest trick is:

In the browser, open Azure Portal fresh

Then look top-right for your profile icon and find:
Switch directory (or “Directories”)

Switch away from Microsoft Services to your own directory (it might be named:

“Default Directory”

or your email name)

If you can’t find it, no stress — once you re-login cleanly, it usually corrects itself.

✅ Step 4 — If you still see “Microsoft Services” tenant problem
Then your account is being forced into a tenant where it doesn’t belong. The fix is:

Option A (most common): Sign out completely
Sign out of Azure Portal

Close all browser tabs

Open Incognito

Sign in again

Option B: You are using a “work/school” tenant you don’t control
If you signed in using a work/school account (company/university), you may not have permission.
In that case:

use a personal Microsoft account for Azure OR

ask that organization admin to add you as a guest (but you don’t need this for your own project)

Yep — that message is consistent with what you’re seeing.

What’s going on (simple)
Azure has 2 “types” of identities:

Personal Microsoft account (Outlook/Hotmail/Gmail login)

Work/School account (Microsoft Entra ID / Azure AD)

When you sign into Azure with a personal account, Azure sometimes drops you into a default tenant called “Microsoft Services”. That tenant has no directory tied to you, so you get the exact error you saw (“account does not exist in tenant Microsoft Services…”). 
Microsoft Learn
+1

Also, some Azure login routes will only accept a work/school account, which is why the #@common trick didn’t work for you.

The fix: create your own Azure directory/subscription first (so you’re not stuck in “Microsoft Services”)
Step 1 — Use the normal portal (not the #@common link)
Open Incognito/InPrivate window

Open Azure Portal normally:

https://portal.azure.com
Sign in with your personal account.

Step 2 — Create an Azure subscription with your personal account
You need to do the “Azure Free account / Pay-As-You-Go” signup once. That signup creates your Default Directory (your tenant) + subscription, and after that the portal works normally.

Open this signup page while logged into your personal account:

https://azure.microsoft.com/free
(After you finish, Azure will create a subscription + your own directory.)

Option A (recommended): create a free Microsoft 365 Developer tenant (gives you a work account)
This gives you a work/school login (like you@something.onmicrosoft.com) that Azure loves, and you can still run everything yourself.

Option B: create an Entra tenant and user (work account) and use that for Azure
Same idea: you’ll have a work account for Azure, and your personal account can remain separate.

i want to also learn as i am building this project, explain me like a 10 yo please bro 
ChatGPT said:
Awesome — and yes, I’ll explain it like you’re 10. 🙂

Think of Azure like a big online computer factory. You’re building a small “robot” inside it that can read invoices.

Here’s what each field you filled means:

1) Subscription = “Who pays the bill?”
Imagine Azure is a shop. A subscription is like your wallet/account in that shop.

Everything you create in Azure gets charged to a subscription.

Even if you choose Free (F0), Azure still wants to know which wallet it belongs to.

So “Default subscription” = your main Azure wallet.

2) Resource Group = “A folder to keep things together”
A resource group is like a big folder where you keep all project stuff together.

Example:

Your project is “Factur-X”

So you create a folder called: facturx-rg

Later you may add:

Document Intelligence (OCR)

Storage (save PDFs)

Database

Web app hosting

If they all live inside the same folder, it’s super easy to manage or delete later.

3) Region = “Where your Azure computer lives”
Region means which country/area Azure will process your data in.

Example: West Europe / France Central.

Why it matters:

Speed: closer region = faster

Rules: for France/EU compliance, you usually prefer EU regions

So you chose a good region.

4) Name = “The unique name tag”
Azure needs a name that is unique (like a username).

That’s why facturx-docint-001 is good.
If someone else already used the same name, Azure won’t allow it.

5) Pricing tier = F0 (Free) = “Free trial mode”
This is the important one.

F0 = free testing mode

It has limits (like “only a few pages/calls per month”)

Perfect for building and testing

Later, when you have customers, you’ll switch to paid tier.

✅ What’s next (1 step only): Get your “Endpoint” and “Key”
Now that the resource is created, Azure gives you 2 secret things:

Endpoint = the “address” of your invoice-reading robot
Like: “This is the URL where the robot lives.”

Key = the “password” to talk to the robot
Only someone with the key can use the service (like a secret door key).

import os
import io
from dotenv import load_dotenv
from azure.core.credentials import AzureKeyCredential
from azure.ai.documentintelligence import DocumentIntelligenceClient


def main():
    load_dotenv()

    endpoint = os.getenv("DOCUMENTINTELLIGENCE_ENDPOINT")
    key = os.getenv("DOCUMENTINTELLIGENCE_API_KEY")

    if not endpoint or not key:
        print("❌ Missing DOCUMENTINTELLIGENCE_ENDPOINT or DOCUMENTINTELLIGENCE_API_KEY in .env")
        return

    client = DocumentIntelligenceClient(endpoint=endpoint, credential=AzureKeyCredential(key))

    pdf_path = r"input\sample_invoice.pdf"   # <-- use your real pdf path if different
    with open(pdf_path, "rb") as f:
        pdf_bytes = f.read()

    poller = client.begin_analyze_document(
        model_id="prebuilt-invoice",
        body=io.BytesIO(pdf_bytes),
    )
    result = poller.result()

    if not result.documents:
        print("❌ No invoice document detected")
        return

    doc = result.documents[0]
    fields = doc.fields or {}

    print("\n✅ Azure extracted fields:")
    for k, v in fields.items():
        # v has value + confidence, we just print "content" (what Azure saw)
        try:
            content = v.get("content")
        except Exception:
            content = str(v)
        print(f"- {k}: {content}")


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
